    35	// Allocate 32 digits for the line number.
    36	// An estimate is that we can print about 1e8 lines/seconds, so 32 digits
    37	// would be enough for billions of universe lifetimes.
    38	const LINE_NUMBER_BUF_SIZE: usize = 32;
    39	
    40	struct LineNumber {
    41	    buf: [u8; LINE_NUMBER_BUF_SIZE],
    42	    print_start: usize,
    43	    num_start: usize,
    44	    num_end: usize,
    45	}
    46	
    47	// Logic to store a string for the line number. Manually incrementing the value
    48	// represented in a buffer like this is significantly faster than storing
    49	// a `usize` and using the standard Rust formatting macros to format a `usize`
    50	// to a string each time it's needed.
    51	// Buffer is initialized to "     1\t" and incremented each time `increment` is
    52	// called, using uucore's fast_inc function that operates on strings.
    53	impl LineNumber {
    54	    fn new() -> Self {
    55	        let mut buf = [b'0'; LINE_NUMBER_BUF_SIZE];
    56	
    57	        let init_str = "     1\t";
    58	        let print_start = buf.len() - init_str.len();
    59	        let num_start = buf.len() - 2;
    60	        let num_end = buf.len() - 1;
    61	
    62	        buf[print_start..].copy_from_slice(init_str.as_bytes());
    63	
    64	        LineNumber {
    65	            buf,
    66	            print_start,
    67	            num_start,
    68	            num_end,
    69	        }
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    fn increment(&mut self) {
    73	        fast_inc_one(&mut self.buf, &mut self.num_start, self.num_end);
    74	        self.print_start = self.print_start.min(self.num_start);
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    #[inline]
    78	    fn to_str(&self) -> &[u8] {
    79	        &self.buf[self.print_start..]
    80	    }
    81	
    82	    fn write(&self, writer: &mut impl Write) -> io::Result<()> {
    83	        writer.write_all(self.to_str())
    84	    }
    85	}
    86	
    87	#[derive(Error, Debug)]
    88	enum CatError {
    89	    /// Wrapper around `io::Error`
    90	    #[error("{0}")]
    91	    Io(#[from] io::Error),
    92	    /// Wrapper around `nix::Error`
    93	    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    94	    #[error("{0}")]
    95	    Nix(#[from] nix::Error),
    96	    /// Unknown file type; it's not a regular file, socket, etc.
    97	    #[error("unknown filetype: {ft_debug}")]
    98	    UnknownFiletype {
    99	        /// A debug print of the file type
   100	        ft_debug: String,
   101	    },
   102	    #[error("Is a directory")]
   103	    IsDirectory,
   104	    #[error("input file is output file")]
   105	    OutputIsInput,
   106	    #[error("Too many levels of symbolic links")]
   107	    TooManySymlinks,
   108	}
   109	
   110	type CatResult<T> = Result<T, CatError>;
   111	
   112	#[derive(PartialEq)]
   113	enum NumberingMode {
   114	    None,
   115	    NonEmpty,
   116	    All,
   117	}
   118	
   119	struct OutputOptions {
   120	    /// Line numbering mode
   121	    number: NumberingMode,
   122	
   123	    /// Suppress repeated empty output lines
   124	    squeeze_blank: bool,
   125	
   126	    /// display TAB characters as `tab`
   127	    show_tabs: bool,
   128	
   129	    /// Show end of lines
   130	    show_ends: bool,
   131	
   132	    /// use ^ and M- notation, except for LF (\\n) and TAB (\\t)
   133	    show_nonprint: bool,
   134	}
   135	
   136	impl OutputOptions {
   137	    fn tab(&self) -> &'static str {
   138	        if self.show_tabs { "^I" } else { "\t" }
   139	    }
   140	
   141	    fn end_of_line(&self) -> &'static str {
   142	        if self.show_ends { "$\n" } else { "\n" }
   143	    }
   144	
   145	    /// We can write fast if we can simply copy the contents of the file to
   146	    /// stdout, without augmenting the output with e.g. line numbers.
   147	    fn can_write_fast(&self) -> bool {
   148	        !(self.show_tabs
   149	            || self.show_nonprint
   150	            || self.show_ends
   151	            || self.squeeze_blank
   152	            || self.number != NumberingMode::None)
   153	    }
   154	}
   155	
   156	/// State that persists between output of each file. This struct is only used
   157	/// when we can't write fast.
   158	struct OutputState {
   159	    /// The current line number
   160	    line_number: LineNumber,
   161	
   162	    /// Whether the output cursor is at the beginning of a new line
   163	    at_line_start: bool,
   164	
   165	    /// Whether we skipped a \r, which still needs to be printed
   166	    skipped_carriage_return: bool,
   167	
   168	    /// Whether we have already printed a blank line
   169	    one_blank_kept: bool,
   170	}
   171	
   172	#[cfg(unix)]
   173	trait FdReadable: Read + AsFd {}
   174	#[cfg(not(unix))]
   175	trait FdReadable: Read {}
   176	
   177	#[cfg(unix)]
   178	impl<T> FdReadable for T where T: Read + AsFd {}
   179	#[cfg(not(unix))]
   180	impl<T> FdReadable for T where T: Read {}
   181	
   182	/// Represents an open file handle, stream, or other device
   183	struct InputHandle<R: FdReadable> {
   184	    reader: R,
   185	    is_interactive: bool,
   186	}

   188	/// Concrete enum of recognized file types.
   189	///
   190	/// *Note*: `cat`-ing a directory should result in an
   191	/// [`CatError::IsDirectory`]
   192	enum InputType {
   193	    Directory,
   194	    File,
   195	    StdIn,
   196	    SymLink,
   197	    #[cfg(unix)]
   198	    BlockDevice,
   199	    #[cfg(unix)]
   200	    CharacterDevice,
   201	    #[cfg(unix)]
   202	    Fifo,
   203	    #[cfg(unix)]
   204	    Socket,
   205	}

   207	mod options {
   208	    pub static FILE: &str = "file";
   209	    pub static SHOW_ALL: &str = "show-all";
   210	    pub static NUMBER_NONBLANK: &str = "number-nonblank";
   211	    pub static SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS: &str = "e";
   212	    pub static SHOW_ENDS: &str = "show-ends";
   213	    pub static NUMBER: &str = "number";
   214	    pub static SQUEEZE_BLANK: &str = "squeeze-blank";
   215	    pub static SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS: &str = "t";
   216	    pub static SHOW_TABS: &str = "show-tabs";
   217	    pub static SHOW_NONPRINTING: &str = "show-nonprinting";
   218	    pub static IGNORED_U: &str = "ignored-u";
   219	}

   221	#[uucore::main]
   222	pub fn uumain(args: impl uucore::Args) -> UResult<()> {
   223	    let matches = uu_app().try_get_matches_from(args)?;
   224	
   225	    let number_mode = if matches.get_flag(options::NUMBER_NONBLANK) {
   226	        NumberingMode::NonEmpty
   227	    } else if matches.get_flag(options::NUMBER) {
   228	        NumberingMode::All
   229	    } else {
   230	        NumberingMode::None
   231	    };
   232	
   233	    let show_nonprint = [
   234	        options::SHOW_ALL.to_owned(),
   235	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS.to_owned(),
   236	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS.to_owned(),
   237	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING.to_owned(),
   238	    ]
   239	    .iter()
   240	    .any(|v| matches.get_flag(v));
   241	
   242	    let show_ends = [
   243	        options::SHOW_ENDS.to_owned(),
   244	        options::SHOW_ALL.to_owned(),
   245	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS.to_owned(),
   246	    ]
   247	    .iter()
   248	    .any(|v| matches.get_flag(v));
   249	
   250	    let show_tabs = [
   251	        options::SHOW_ALL.to_owned(),
   252	        options::SHOW_TABS.to_owned(),
   253	        options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS.to_owned(),
   254	    ]
   255	    .iter()
   256	    .any(|v| matches.get_flag(v));
   257	
   258	    let squeeze_blank = matches.get_flag(options::SQUEEZE_BLANK);
   259	    let files: Vec<String> = match matches.get_many::<String>(options::FILE) {
   260	        Some(v) => v.cloned().collect(),
   261	        None => vec!["-".to_owned()],
   262	    };
   263	
   264	    let options = OutputOptions {
   265	        show_ends,
   266	        number: number_mode,
   267	        show_nonprint,
   268	        show_tabs,
   269	        squeeze_blank,
   270	    };
   271	    cat_files(&files, &options)
   272	}
   273	
   274	pub fn uu_app() -> Command {
   275	    Command::new(uucore::util_name())
   276	        .version(uucore::crate_version!())
   277	        .override_usage(format_usage(&get_message("cat-usage")))
   278	        .about(get_message("cat-about"))
   279	        .infer_long_args(true)
   280	        .args_override_self(true)
   281	        .arg(
   282	            Arg::new(options::FILE)
   283	                .hide(true)
   284	                .action(ArgAction::Append)
   285	                .value_hint(clap::ValueHint::FilePath),
   286	        )
   287	        .arg(
   288	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_ALL)
   289	                .short('A')
   290	                .long(options::SHOW_ALL)
   291	                .help("equivalent to -vET")
   292	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   293	        )
   294	        .arg(
   295	            Arg::new(options::NUMBER_NONBLANK)
   296	                .short('b')
   297	                .long(options::NUMBER_NONBLANK)
   298	                .help("number nonempty output lines, overrides -n")
   299	                // Note: This MUST NOT .overrides_with(options::NUMBER)!
   300	                // In clap, overriding is symmetric, so "-b -n" counts as "-n", which is not what we want.
   301	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   302	        )
   303	        .arg(
   304	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_ENDS)
   305	                .short('e')
   306	                .help("equivalent to -vE")
   307	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   308	        )
   309	        .arg(
   310	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_ENDS)
   311	                .short('E')
   312	                .long(options::SHOW_ENDS)
   313	                .help("display $ at end of each line")
   314	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   315	        )
   316	        .arg(
   317	            Arg::new(options::NUMBER)
   318	                .short('n')
   319	                .long(options::NUMBER)
   320	                .help("number all output lines")
   321	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   322	        )
   323	        .arg(
   324	            Arg::new(options::SQUEEZE_BLANK)
   325	                .short('s')
   326	                .long(options::SQUEEZE_BLANK)
   327	                .help("suppress repeated empty output lines")
   328	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   329	        )
   330	        .arg(
   331	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING_TABS)
   332	                .short('t')
   333	                .help("equivalent to -vT")
   334	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   335	        )
   336	        .arg(
   337	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_TABS)
   338	                .short('T')
   339	                .long(options::SHOW_TABS)
   340	                .help("display TAB characters at ^I")
   341	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   342	        )
   343	        .arg(
   344	            Arg::new(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING)
   345	                .short('v')
   346	                .long(options::SHOW_NONPRINTING)
   347	                .help("use ^ and M- notation, except for LF (\\n) and TAB (\\t)")
   348	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   349	        )
   350	        .arg(
   351	            Arg::new(options::IGNORED_U)
   352	                .short('u')
   353	                .help("(ignored)")
   354	                .action(ArgAction::SetTrue),
   355	        )
   356	}
   357	
   358	fn cat_handle<R: FdReadable>(
   359	    handle: &mut InputHandle<R>,
   360	    options: &OutputOptions,
   361	    state: &mut OutputState,
   362	) -> CatResult<()> {
   363	    if options.can_write_fast() {
   364	        write_fast(handle)
   365	    } else {
   366	        write_lines(handle, options, state)
   367	    }
   368	}
   369	
   370	fn cat_path(path: &str, options: &OutputOptions, state: &mut OutputState) -> CatResult<()> {
   371	    match get_input_type(path)? {
   372	        InputType::StdIn => {
   373	            let stdin = io::stdin();
   374	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&stdin, &io::stdout()) {
   375	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   376	            }
   377	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   378	                reader: stdin,
   379	                is_interactive: io::stdin().is_terminal(),
   380	            };
   381	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   382	        }
   383	        InputType::Directory => Err(CatError::IsDirectory),
   384	        #[cfg(unix)]
   385	        InputType::Socket => {
   386	            let socket = UnixStream::connect(path)?;
   387	            socket.shutdown(Shutdown::Write)?;
   388	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   389	                reader: socket,
   390	                is_interactive: false,
   391	            };
   392	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   393	        }
   394	        _ => {
   395	            let file = File::open(path)?;
   396	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&file, &io::stdout()) {
   397	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   398	            }
   399	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   400	                reader: file,
   401	                is_interactive: false,
   402	            };
   403	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   404	        }
   405	    }
   406	}
   407	
   408	fn cat_files(files: &[String], options: &OutputOptions) -> UResult<()> {
   409	    let mut state = OutputState {
   410	        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
   411	        at_line_start: true,
   412	        skipped_carriage_return: false,
   413	        one_blank_kept: false,
   414	    };
   415	    let mut error_messages: Vec<String> = Vec::new();
   416	
   417	    for path in files {
   418	        if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
   419	            error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
   420	        }
   421	    }
   422	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   423	        print!("\r");
   424	    }
   425	    if error_messages.is_empty() {
   426	        Ok(())
   427	    } else {
   428	        // each next line is expected to display "cat: …"
   429	        let line_joiner = format!("\n{}: ", uucore::util_name());
   430	
   431	        Err(uucore::error::USimpleError::new(
   432	            error_messages.len() as i32,
   433	            error_messages.join(&line_joiner),
   434	        ))
   435	    }
   436	}
   437	
   438	/// Classifies the `InputType` of file at `path` if possible
   439	///
   440	/// # Arguments
   441	///
   442	/// * `path` - Path on a file system to classify metadata
   443	fn get_input_type(path: &str) -> CatResult<InputType> {
   444	    if path == "-" {
   445	        return Ok(InputType::StdIn);
   446	    }
   447	
   448	    let ft = match metadata(path) {
   449	        Ok(md) => md.file_type(),
   450	        Err(e) => {
   451	            if let Some(raw_error) = e.raw_os_error() {
   452	                // On Unix-like systems, the error code for "Too many levels of symbolic links" is 40 (ELOOP).
   453	                // we want to provide a proper error message in this case.
   454	                #[cfg(not(any(target_os = "macos", target_os = "freebsd")))]
   455	                let too_many_symlink_code = 40;
   456	                #[cfg(any(target_os = "macos", target_os = "freebsd"))]
   457	                let too_many_symlink_code = 62;
   458	                if raw_error == too_many_symlink_code {
   459	                    return Err(CatError::TooManySymlinks);
   460	                }
   461	            }
   462	            return Err(CatError::Io(e));
   463	        }
   464	    };
   465	    match ft {
   466	        #[cfg(unix)]
   467	        ft if ft.is_block_device() => Ok(InputType::BlockDevice),
   468	        #[cfg(unix)]
   469	        ft if ft.is_char_device() => Ok(InputType::CharacterDevice),
   470	        #[cfg(unix)]
   471	        ft if ft.is_fifo() => Ok(InputType::Fifo),
   472	        #[cfg(unix)]
   473	        ft if ft.is_socket() => Ok(InputType::Socket),
   474	        ft if ft.is_dir() => Ok(InputType::Directory),
   475	        ft if ft.is_file() => Ok(InputType::File),
   476	        ft if ft.is_symlink() => Ok(InputType::SymLink),
   477	        _ => Err(CatError::UnknownFiletype {
   478	            ft_debug: format!("{ft:?}"),
   479	        }),
   480	    }
   481	}
   482	
   483	/// Writes handle to stdout with no configuration. This allows a
   484	/// simple memory copy.
   485	fn write_fast<R: FdReadable>(handle: &mut InputHandle<R>) -> CatResult<()> {
   486	    let stdout = io::stdout();
   487	    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
   488	    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
   489	    {
   490	        // If we're on Linux or Android, try to use the splice() system call
   491	        // for faster writing. If it works, we're done.
   492	        if !splice::write_fast_using_splice(handle, &stdout_lock)? {
   493	            return Ok(());
   494	        }
   495	    }
   496	    // If we're not on Linux or Android, or the splice() call failed,
   497	    // fall back on slower writing.
   498	    let mut buf = [0; 1024 * 64];
   499	    loop {
   500	        match handle.reader.read(&mut buf) {
   501	            Ok(n) => {
   502	                if n == 0 {
   503	                    break;
   504	                }
   505	                stdout_lock.write_all(&buf[..n])?;
   506	            }
   507	            Err(e) => return Err(e.into()),
   508	        }
   509	    }
   510	
   511	    // If the splice() call failed and there has been some data written to
   512	    // stdout via while loop above AND there will be second splice() call
   513	    // that will succeed, data pushed through splice will be output before
   514	    // the data buffered in stdout.lock. Therefore additional explicit flush
   515	    // is required here.
   516	    stdout_lock.flush()?;
   517	    Ok(())
   518	}
   519	
   520	/// Outputs file contents to stdout in a line-by-line fashion,
   521	/// propagating any errors that might occur.
   522	fn write_lines<R: FdReadable>(
   523	    handle: &mut InputHandle<R>,
   524	    options: &OutputOptions,
   525	    state: &mut OutputState,

str_replace_editor create /testbed/test_epipe.py --file_text '#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Test script to reproduce the EPIPE issue with cat reading from /dev/zero"""

import subprocess
import os
import sys

def test_epipe_issue():
    """Test if cat handles EPIPE error when reading from /dev/zero"""
    
    # Test 1: Normal cat /dev/zero | head -c 10
    print("Test 1: cat /dev/zero | head -c 10")
    try:
        result = subprocess.run(
            "cat /dev/zero | head -c 10",
            shell=True,
            capture_output=True,
            text=True
        )
        print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
        print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
        print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr}")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"  Error: {e}")
    
    print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
    
    # Test 2: Using uutils cat specifically
    print("Test 2: Using uutils cat built from this repo")
    
    # First, let'"'"'s build the uutils cat
    print("Building uutils cat...")
    build_result = subprocess.run(
        ["cargo", "build", "--release", "--bin", "cat"],
        cwd="/testbed",
        capture_output=True,
        text=True
    )
    
    if build_result.returncode != 0:
        print(f"Build failed: {build_result.stderr}")
        return
    
    print("Build successful!")
    
    # Test with uutils cat
    cat_path = "/testbed/target/release/cat"
    
    if not os.path.exists(cat_path):
        # Try debug build
        cat_path = "/testbed/target/debug/cat"
        if not os.path.exists(cat_path):
            print("Could not find built cat binary")
            return
    
    print(f"Using cat binary: {cat_path}")
    
    try:
        result = subprocess.run(
            f"{cat_path} /dev/zero | head -c 10",
            shell=True,
            capture_output=True,
            text=True
        )
        print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
        print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
        if result.stderr:
            print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr}")
        else:
            print("  No stderr output")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"  Error: {e}")
    
    print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
    
    # Test 3: Compare with GNU cat
    print("Test 3: Using GNU cat for comparison")
    try:
        result = subprocess.run(
            "cat /dev/zero | head -c 10",
            shell=True,
            capture_output=True,
            text=True
        )
        print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
        print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
        if result.stderr:
            print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr}")
        else:
            print("  No stderr output")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"  Error: {e}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    test_epipe_issue()'

Now I understand the issue! The problem is in line 505 where `stdout_lock.write_all(&buf[..n])?;` is called. When the pipe is broken (EPIPE), this operation fails and the `?` operator propagates the error up, which eventually gets printed as an error message.

In GNU cat, when a broken pipe (EPIPE) occurs, it's handled gracefully by exiting silently rather than printing an error message. This is the expected behavior for Unix utilities when the reader of a pipe closes the connection.

Let me check how other utilities handle EPIPE errors in uutils:

use std::io;

fn main() {
    // Check EPIPE error code
    let epipe_error = io::Error::from_raw_os_error(32); // EPIPE is typically 32
    println!("EPIPE error: {}", epipe_error);
    
    // Check if we can match on error kind
    match epipe_error.kind() {
        io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe => {
            println!("EPIPE matches ErrorKind::BrokenPipe");
        }
        _ => {
            println!("EPIPE does not match BrokenPipe");
        }
    }
}'

use std::io;
use std::io::Write;

fn main() {
    // Test how write_all behaves with EPIPE
    let stdout = io::stdout();
    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
    
    // Write to stdout and see what happens
    let test_data = [42u8; 4096];
    
    match stdout_lock.write_all(&test_data) {
        Ok(_) => println!("Write successful"),
        Err(e) => {
            println!("Write error: {}", e);
            if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                println!("This is a broken pipe error");
            }
        }
    }
}'

Now I need to fix the EPIPE issue. The problem is in lines 505 and 516 where `write_all` and `flush` are used with the `?` operator. When a broken pipe (EPIPE) occurs, these operations fail and the error is propagated up, eventually being printed as an error message.

The fix is to handle `io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe` specifically by exiting gracefully (returning `Ok(())`) instead of propagating the error. This matches the behavior of GNU cat.

Let me implement the fix:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/cat/src/cat.rs   --old_str 'fn write_fast<R: FdReadable>(handle: &mut InputHandle<R>) -> CatResult<()> {
    let stdout = io::stdout();
    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    {
        // If we'"'"'re on Linux or Android, try to use the splice() system call
        // for faster writing. If it works, we'"'"'re done.
        if !splice::write_fast_using_splice(handle, &stdout_lock)? {
            return Ok(());
        }
    }
    // If we'"'"'re not on Linux or Android, or the splice() call failed,
    // fall back on slower writing.
    let mut buf = [0; 1024 * 64];
    loop {
        match handle.reader.read(&mut buf) {
            Ok(n) => {
                if n == 0 {
                    break;
                }
                stdout_lock.write_all(&buf[..n])?;
            }
            Err(e) => return Err(e.into()),
        }
    }

    // If the splice() call failed and there has been some data written to
    // stdout via while loop above AND there will be second splice() call
    // that will succeed, data pushed through splice will be output before
    // the data buffered in stdout.lock. Therefore additional explicit flush
    // is required here.
    stdout_lock.flush()?;
    Ok(())
}' --new_str 'fn write_fast<R: FdReadable>(handle: &mut InputHandle<R>) -> CatResult<()> {
    let stdout = io::stdout();
    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
    #[cfg(any(target_os = "linux", target_os = "android"))]
    {
        // If we'"'"'re on Linux or Android, try to use the splice() system call
        // for faster writing. If it works, we'"'"'re done.
        if !splice::write_fast_using_splice(handle, &stdout_lock)? {
            return Ok(());
        }
    }
    // If we'"'"'re not on Linux or Android, or the splice() call failed,
    // fall back on slower writing.
    let mut buf = [0; 1024 * 64];
    loop {
        match handle.reader.read(&mut buf) {
            Ok(n) => {
                if n == 0 {
                    break;
                }
                // Handle broken pipe errors gracefully
                if let Err(e) = stdout_lock.write_all(&buf[..n]) {
                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
                        return Ok(());
                    } else {
                        return Err(e.into());
                    }
                }
            }
            Err(e) => return Err(e.into()),
        }
    }

    // If the splice() call failed and there has been some data written to
    // stdout via while loop above AND there will be second splice() call
    // that will succeed, data pushed through splice will be output before
    // the data buffered in stdout.lock. Therefore additional explicit flush
    // is required here.
    // Handle broken pipe errors gracefully for flush as well
    if let Err(e) = stdout_lock.flush() {
        if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
            // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
            return Ok(());
        } else {
            return Err(e.into());
        }
    }
    Ok(())
}'

   536	/// Outputs file contents to stdout in a line-by-line fashion,
   537	/// propagating any errors that might occur.
   538	fn write_lines<R: FdReadable>(
   539	    handle: &mut InputHandle<R>,
   540	    options: &OutputOptions,
   541	    state: &mut OutputState,
   542	) -> CatResult<()> {
   543	    let mut in_buf = [0; 1024 * 31];
   544	    let stdout = io::stdout();
   545	    let stdout = stdout.lock();
   546	    // Add a 32K buffer for stdout - this greatly improves performance.
   547	    let mut writer = BufWriter::with_capacity(32 * 1024, stdout);
   548	
   549	    while let Ok(n) = handle.reader.read(&mut in_buf) {
   550	        if n == 0 {
   551	            break;
   552	        }
   553	        let in_buf = &in_buf[..n];
   554	        let mut pos = 0;
   555	        while pos < n {
   556	            // skip empty line_number enumerating them if needed
   557	            if in_buf[pos] == b'\n' {
   558	                write_new_line(&mut writer, options, state, handle.is_interactive)?;
   559	                state.at_line_start = true;
   560	                pos += 1;
   561	                continue;
   562	            }
   563	            if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   564	                writer.write_all(b"\r")?;
   565	                state.skipped_carriage_return = false;
   566	                state.at_line_start = false;
   567	            }
   568	            state.one_blank_kept = false;
   569	            if state.at_line_start && options.number != NumberingMode::None {
   570	                state.line_number.write(&mut writer)?;
   571	                state.line_number.increment();
   572	            }
   573	
   574	            // print to end of line or end of buffer
   575	            let offset = write_end(&mut writer, &in_buf[pos..], options);
   576	
   577	            // end of buffer?
   578	            if offset + pos == in_buf.len() {
   579	                state.at_line_start = false;
   580	                break;
   581	            }
   582	            if in_buf[pos + offset] == b'\r' {
   583	                state.skipped_carriage_return = true;
   584	            } else {
   585	                assert_eq!(in_buf[pos + offset], b'\n');
   586	                // print suitable end of line
   587	                write_end_of_line(
   588	                    &mut writer,
   589	                    options.end_of_line().as_bytes(),
   590	                    handle.is_interactive,
   591	                )?;
   592	                state.at_line_start = true;
   593	            }
   594	            pos += offset + 1;
   595	        }
   596	        // We need to flush the buffer each time around the loop in order to pass GNU tests.
   597	        // When we are reading the input from a pipe, the `handle.reader.read` call at the top
   598	        // of this loop will block (indefinitely) whist waiting for more data. The expectation
   599	        // however is that anything that's ready for output should show up in the meantime,
   600	        // and not be buffered internally to the `cat` process.
   601	        // Hence it's necessary to flush our buffer before every time we could potentially block
   602	        // on a `std::io::Read::read` call.
   603	        writer.flush()?;
   604	    }
   605	
   606	    Ok(())
   607	}
   608	
   609	/// `\r` followed by `\n` is printed as `^M` when `show_ends` is enabled, so that `\r\n` prints as `^M$`
   610	fn write_new_line<W: Write>(
   611	    writer: &mut W,
   612	    options: &OutputOptions,
   613	    state: &mut OutputState,
   614	    is_interactive: bool,
   615	) -> CatResult<()> {
   616	    if state.skipped_carriage_return {
   617	        if options.show_ends {
   618	            writer.write_all(b"^M")?;
   619	        } else {
   620	            writer.write_all(b"\r")?;
   621	        }
   622	        state.skipped_carriage_return = false;
   623	
   624	        write_end_of_line(writer, options.end_of_line().as_bytes(), is_interactive)?;
   625	        return Ok(());
   626	    }
   627	    if !state.at_line_start || !options.squeeze_blank || !state.one_blank_kept {
   628	        state.one_blank_kept = true;
   629	        if state.at_line_start && options.number == NumberingMode::All {
   630	            state.line_number.write(writer)?;
   631	            state.line_number.increment();
   632	        }
   633	        write_end_of_line(writer, options.end_of_line().as_bytes(), is_interactive)?;
   634	    }
   635	    Ok(())
   636	}
   637	
   638	fn write_end<W: Write>(writer: &mut W, in_buf: &[u8], options: &OutputOptions) -> usize {
   639	    if options.show_nonprint {
   640	        write_nonprint_to_end(in_buf, writer, options.tab().as_bytes())
   641	    } else if options.show_tabs {
   642	        write_tab_to_end(in_buf, writer)
   643	    } else {
   644	        write_to_end(in_buf, writer)
   645	    }
   646	}
   647	
   648	// write***_to_end methods
   649	// Write all symbols till \n or \r or end of buffer is reached
   650	// We need to stop at \r because it may be written as ^M depending on the byte after and settings;
   651	// however, write_nonprint_to_end doesn't need to stop at \r because it will always write \r as ^M.
   652	// Return the number of written symbols
   653	
   654	fn write_to_end<W: Write>(in_buf: &[u8], writer: &mut W) -> usize {
   655	    // using memchr2 significantly improves performances
   656	    match memchr2(b'\n', b'\r', in_buf) {
   657	        Some(p) => {
   658	            writer.write_all(&in_buf[..p]).unwrap();
   659	            p
   660	        }

Now I understand the issue completely. The problem is that uutils `cat` doesn't handle broken pipe (EPIPE) errors gracefully. When writing to stdout and the pipe is broken (e.g., when the reader like `head` closes the pipe), the `write_all` and `flush` operations fail with EPIPE, and these errors are propagated up and printed as error messages.

GNU `cat`, on the other hand, handles EPIPE errors gracefully by exiting silently, which is the expected behavior for Unix utilities.

"""Helper to fix all EPIPE handling in cat.rs"""

import re

def fix_write_operations(content):
    """Fix write operations to handle EPIPE gracefully"""
    
    # Pattern to find write_all and flush calls that use `?` operator
    # This indicates they'"'"'re propagating errors but not handling EPIPE
    patterns = [
        r'"'"'(\s+)(\w+\.write_all\([^)]+\))\?'"'"',
        r'"'"'(\s+)(\w+\.flush\(\))\?'"'"'
    ]
    
    for pattern in patterns:
        # Replace pattern with EPIPE handling
        replacement = r'"'"'\1if let Err(e) = \2 {\n\1    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {\n\1        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat\n\1        return Ok(());\n\1    } else {\n\1        return Err(e.into());\n\1    }\n\1}'"'"'
        content = re.sub(pattern, replacement, content)
    
    return content

# Apply the fix

    content = f.read()

# Fix the write operations we identified earlier

                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
                        return Ok(());
                    } else {
                        return Err(e.into());
                    }
                }'"'"''"'"''"'"')

                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
                        return Ok(());
                    } else {
                        return Err(e.into());
                    }
                }'"'"''"'"''"'"')

                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
                        return Ok(());
                    } else {
                        return Err(e.into());
                    }
                }'"'"''"'"''"'"')

# Fix the write_end_of_line function
old_write_end_of_line = '"'"''"'"''"'"'fn write_end_of_line<W: Write>(
    writer: &mut W,
    end_of_line: &[u8],
    is_interactive: bool,
) -> CatResult<()> {
    writer.write_all(end_of_line)?;
    if is_interactive {
        writer.flush()?;
    }
    Ok(())
}'"'"''"'"''"'"'

new_write_end_of_line = '"'"''"'"''"'"'fn write_end_of_line<W: Write>(
    writer: &mut W,
    end_of_line: &[u8],
    is_interactive: bool,
) -> CatResult<()> {
    if let Err(e) = writer.write_all(end_of_line) {
        if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
            // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
            return Ok(());
        } else {
            return Err(e.into());
        }
    }
    if is_interactive {
        if let Err(e) = writer.flush() {
            if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
                return Ok(());
            } else {
                return Err(e.into());
            }
        }
    }
    Ok(())
}'"'"''"'"''"'"'

content = content.replace(old_write_end_of_line, new_write_end_of_line)

old_pattern = r'"'"'(\s+)state\.line_number\.write\(&mut writer\)\?'"'"'
replacement = r'"'"'\1if let Err(e) = state.line_number.write(&mut writer) {\n\1    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {\n\1        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat\n\1        return Ok(());\n\1    } else {\n\1        return Err(e.into());\n\1    }\n\1}'"'"'
content = re.sub(old_pattern, replacement, content)

with open('"'"'/testbed/src/uu/cat/src/cat.rs'"'"', '"'"'w'"'"') as f:
    f.write(content)

print("Fixed EPIPE handling in cat.rs")'

   758	fn write_end_of_line<W: Write>(
   759	    writer: &mut W,
   760	    end_of_line: &[u8],
   761	    is_interactive: bool,
   762	) -> CatResult<()> {

    let mut count = 0;

    for byte in in_buf.iter().copied() {
        if byte == b'"'"'\n'"'"' {
            break;
        }
        let write_result = match byte {
            9 => writer.write_all(tab),
            0..=8 | 10..=31 => writer.write_all(&[b'"'"'^'"'"', byte + 64]),
            32..=126 => writer.write_all(&[byte]),
            127 => writer.write_all(b"^?"),
            128..=159 => writer.write_all(&[b'"'"'M'"'"', b'"'"'-'"'"', b'"'"'^'"'"', byte - 64]),
            160..=254 => writer.write_all(&[b'"'"'M'"'"', b'"'"'-'"'"', byte - 128]),
            _ => writer.write_all(b"M-^?"),
        };
        
        // Handle broken pipe errors gracefully
        if let Err(e) = write_result {
            if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
                // Since we can'"'"'t return a Result from this function, we need to break the loop
                break;
            } else {
                // For other errors, we can'"'"'t propagate them properly since this function returns usize
                // So we'"'"'ll use unwrap() which will panic, but this preserves the existing behavior for non-EPIPE errors
                panic!("write error: {}", e);
            }
        }
        count += 1;
    }
    count
}'

"""Trace where the EPIPE error is coming from"""

import subprocess
import sys

# Run the command and capture both stdout and stderr separately
cat_path = "/testbed/target/debug/coreutils"

print(f"Running: {cat_path} cat /dev/zero | head -c 10")

# Use Popen to capture stderr separately 
cat_process = subprocess.Popen(
    [cat_path, "cat", "/dev/zero"],
    stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
    stderr=subprocess.PIPE
)

head_process = subprocess.Popen(
    ["head", "-c", "10"],
    stdin=cat_process.stdout,
    stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
    stderr=subprocess.PIPE
)

# Close the stdout of cat process
cat_process.stdout.close()

# Get the output
head_output, head_stderr = head_process.communicate()

# Get the stderr from cat process
cat_stderr = cat_process.stderr.read()

print(f"Head stdout length: {len(head_output)}")
print(f"Head stderr: {head_stderr.decode() if head_stderr else '"'"'None'"'"'}")
print(f"Cat stderr: {cat_stderr.decode() if cat_stderr else '"'"'None'"'"'}")
print(f"Head exit code: {head_process.returncode}")
print(f"Cat exit code: {cat_process.wait()}")'

   409	    let mut state = OutputState {
   410	        line_number: LineNumber::new(),
   411	        at_line_start: true,
   412	        skipped_carriage_return: false,
   413	        one_blank_kept: false,

   370	fn cat_path(path: &str, options: &OutputOptions, state: &mut OutputState) -> CatResult<()> {
   371	    match get_input_type(path)? {
   372	        InputType::StdIn => {
   373	            let stdin = io::stdin();
   374	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&stdin, &io::stdout()) {
   375	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   376	            }
   377	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   378	                reader: stdin,
   379	                is_interactive: io::stdin().is_terminal(),
   380	            };
   381	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   382	        }
   383	        InputType::Directory => Err(CatError::IsDirectory),
   384	        #[cfg(unix)]
   385	        InputType::Socket => {
   386	            let socket = UnixStream::connect(path)?;
   387	            socket.shutdown(Shutdown::Write)?;
   388	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   389	                reader: socket,
   390	                is_interactive: false,
   391	            };
   392	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   393	        }
   394	        _ => {
   395	            let file = File::open(path)?;
   396	            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&file, &io::stdout()) {
   397	                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
   398	            }
   399	            let mut handle = InputHandle {
   400	                reader: file,
   401	                is_interactive: false,
   402	            };
   403	            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
   404	        }
   405	    }

Now I understand the issue! The problem is that even though I'm handling EPIPE errors gracefully in the `write_fast` and `write_lines` functions, the error is still being propagated up through the call chain and eventually being printed by the error handling system in `cat_files`.

The issue is in line 418 of `cat_files` function:
```rust
if let Err(err) = cat_path(path, options, &mut state) {
    error_messages.push(format!("{}: {err}", path.maybe_quote()));
}
```

When `cat_path` returns an error (even an EPIPE error that we've handled gracefully by returning `Ok(())`), it's still being caught and added to the error messages. The problem is that the EPIPE error is being converted to a `CatError::Io` and then propagated up.

Let me check how the error conversion is happening. The issue is that when we return `Err(e.into())` for non-EPIPE errors, the `e.into()` converts the `io::Error` to a `CatError::Io`, which then gets propagated up and printed.

The fix is to handle EPIPE errors at the highest level possible, right before the error is converted to a `CatError`. Let me modify the approach:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/uu/cat/src/cat.rs   --old_str 'fn cat_path(path: &str, options: &OutputOptions, state: &mut OutputState) -> CatResult<()> {
    match get_input_type(path)? {
        InputType::StdIn => {
            let stdin = io::stdin();
            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&stdin, &io::stdout()) {
                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
            }
            let mut handle = InputHandle {
                reader: stdin,
                is_interactive: io::stdin().is_terminal(),
            };
            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
        }
        InputType::Directory => Err(CatError::IsDirectory),
        #[cfg(unix)]
        InputType::Socket => {
            let socket = UnixStream::connect(path)?;
            socket.shutdown(Shutdown::Write)?;
            let mut handle = InputHandle {
                reader: socket,
                is_interactive: false,
            };
            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
        }
        _ => {
            let file = File::open(path)?;
            if is_unsafe_overwrite(&file, &io::stdout()) {
                return Err(CatError::OutputIsInput);
            }
            let mut handle = InputHandle {
                reader: file,
                is_interactive: false,
            };
            cat_handle(&mut handle, options, state)
        }
    }

use std::io::{self, Write};

fn main() {
    let stdout = io::stdout();
    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
    
    // Test writing a single byte and handling EPIPE
    let test_byte = [0u8];
    
    match stdout_lock.write_all(&test_byte) {
        Ok(_) => println!("Write successful"),
        Err(e) => {
            if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                println!("Got broken pipe error");
                std::process::exit(0); // Exit cleanly like GNU cat
            } else {
                eprintln!("Error: {}", e);
                std::process::exit(1);
            }
        }
    }
    
    // If we get here, continue normally
    println!("Continuing after write...");
}'

   130	/// Disables the custom signal handlers installed by Rust for stack-overflow handling. With those custom signal handlers processes ignore the first SIGBUS and SIGSEGV signal they receive.
   131	/// See <https://github.com/rust-lang/rust/blob/8ac1525e091d3db28e67adcbbd6db1e1deaa37fb/src/libstd/sys/unix/stack_overflow.rs#L71-L92> for details.
   132	#[cfg(unix)]
   133	pub fn disable_rust_signal_handlers() -> Result<(), Errno> {
   134	    unsafe {
   135	        sigaction(
   136	            SIGSEGV,
   137	            &SigAction::new(SigDfl, SaFlags::empty(), SigSet::all()),
   138	        )
   139	    }?;
   140	    unsafe {
   141	        sigaction(
   142	            SIGBUS,
   143	            &SigAction::new(SigDfl, SaFlags::empty(), SigSet::all()),
   144	        )
   145	    }?;
   146	    Ok(())
   147	}

   149	pub fn get_canonical_util_name(util_name: &str) -> &str {
   150	    // remove the "uu_" prefix
   151	    let util_name = &util_name[3..];
   152	    match util_name {
   153	        // uu_test aliases - '[' is an alias for test
   154	        "[" => "test",
   155	
   156	        // hashsum aliases - all these hash commands are aliases for hashsum
   157	        "md5sum" | "sha1sum" | "sha224sum" | "sha256sum" | "sha384sum" | "sha512sum"
   158	        | "sha3sum" | "sha3-224sum" | "sha3-256sum" | "sha3-384sum" | "sha3-512sum"
   159	        | "shake128sum" | "shake256sum" | "b2sum" | "b3sum" => "hashsum",
   160	
   161	        "dir" => "ls", // dir is an alias for ls
   162	
   163	        // Default case - return the util name as is
   164	        _ => util_name,
   165	    }
   166	}

   168	/// Execute utility code for `util`.
   169	///
   170	/// This macro expands to a main function that invokes the `uumain` function in `util`
   171	/// Exits with code returned by `uumain`.
   172	#[macro_export]
   173	macro_rules! bin {
   174	    ($util:ident) => {
   175	        pub fn main() {
   176	            use std::io::Write;
   177	            use uucore::locale;
   178	            // suppress extraneous error output for SIGPIPE failures/panics
   179	            uucore::panic::mute_sigpipe_panic();
   180	            locale::setup_localization(uucore::get_canonical_util_name(stringify!($util)))
   181	                .unwrap_or_else(|err| {
   182	                    match err {
   183	                        uucore::locale::LocalizationError::ParseResource {
   184	                            error: err_msg,
   185	                            snippet,
   186	                        } => eprintln!("Localization parse error at {snippet}: {err_msg}"),
   187	                        other => eprintln!("Could not init the localization system: {other}"),
   188	                    }
   189	                    std::process::exit(99)
   190	                });
   191	
   192	            // execute utility code
   193	            let code = $util::uumain(uucore::args_os());
   194	            // (defensively) flush stdout for utility prior to exit; see <https://github.com/rust-lang/rust/issues/23818>
   195	            if let Err(e) = std::io::stdout().flush() {
   196	                eprintln!("Error flushing stdout: {e}");
   197	            }
   198	
   199	            std::process::exit(code);
   200	        }
   201	    };
   202	}

   204	/// Generate the version string for clap.
   205	///
   206	/// The generated string has the format `(<project name>) <version>`, for
   207	/// example: "(uutils coreutils) 0.30.0". clap will then prefix it with the util name.
   208	///
   209	/// To use this macro, you have to add `PROJECT_NAME_FOR_VERSION_STRING = "<project name>"` to the
   210	/// `[env]` section in `.cargo/config.toml`.
   211	#[macro_export]
   212	macro_rules! crate_version {
   213	    () => {
   214	        concat!(
   215	            "(",
   216	            env!("PROJECT_NAME_FOR_VERSION_STRING"),
   217	            ") ",
   218	            env!("CARGO_PKG_VERSION")
   219	        )
   220	    };
   221	}
   222	
   223	/// Generate the usage string for clap.
   224	///
   225	/// This function does two things. It indents all but the first line to align
   226	/// the lines because clap adds "Usage: " to the first line. And it replaces
   227	/// all occurrences of `{}` with the execution phrase and returns the resulting
   228	/// `String`. It does **not** support more advanced formatting features such
   229	/// as `{0}`.
   230	pub fn format_usage(s: &str) -> String {
   231	    let s = s.replace('\n', &format!("\n{}", " ".repeat(7)));
   232	    s.replace("{}", crate::execution_phrase())
   233	}

   235	/// Used to check if the utility is the second argument.
   236	/// Used to check if we were called as a multicall binary (`coreutils <utility>`)
   237	pub fn get_utility_is_second_arg() -> bool {
   238	    crate::macros::UTILITY_IS_SECOND_ARG.load(Ordering::SeqCst)
   239	}

   241	/// Change the value of `UTILITY_IS_SECOND_ARG` to true
   242	/// Used to specify that the utility is the second argument.

   244	    crate::macros::UTILITY_IS_SECOND_ARG.store(true, Ordering::SeqCst);
   245	}
   246	
   247	// args_os() can be expensive to call, it copies all of argv before iterating.
   248	// So if we want only the first arg or so it's overkill. We cache it.
   249	static ARGV: LazyLock<Vec<OsString>> = LazyLock::new(|| wild::args_os().collect());
   250	
   251	static UTIL_NAME: LazyLock<String> = LazyLock::new(|| {
   252	    let base_index = usize::from(get_utility_is_second_arg());
   253	    let is_man = usize::from(ARGV[base_index].eq("manpage"));
   254	    let argv_index = base_index + is_man;
   255	
   256	    ARGV[argv_index].to_string_lossy().into_owned()
   257	});
   258	
   259	/// Derive the utility name.
   260	pub fn util_name() -> &'static str {
   261	    &UTIL_NAME
   262	}
   263	
   264	static EXECUTION_PHRASE: LazyLock<String> = LazyLock::new(|| {
   265	    if get_utility_is_second_arg() {
   266	        ARGV.iter()
   267	            .take(2)
   268	            .map(|os_str| os_str.to_string_lossy().into_owned())
   269	            .collect::<Vec<_>>()
   270	            .join(" ")
   271	    } else {
   272	        ARGV[0].to_string_lossy().into_owned()
   273	    }
   274	});
   275	
   276	/// Derive the complete execution phrase for "usage".
   277	pub fn execution_phrase() -> &'static str {
   278	    &EXECUTION_PHRASE
   279	}
   280	
   281	/// Args contains arguments passed to the utility.
   282	/// It is a trait that extends `Iterator<Item = OsString>`.
   283	/// It provides utility functions to collect the arguments into a `Vec<String>`.
   284	/// The collected `Vec<String>` can be lossy or ignore invalid encoding.
   285	pub trait Args: Iterator<Item = OsString> + Sized {
   286	    /// Collects the iterator into a `Vec<String>`, lossily converting the `OsString`s to `Strings`.
   287	    fn collect_lossy(self) -> Vec<String> {
   288	        self.map(|s| s.to_string_lossy().into_owned()).collect()
   289	    }
   290	
   291	    /// Collects the iterator into a `Vec<String>`, removing any elements that contain invalid encoding.
   292	    fn collect_ignore(self) -> Vec<String> {
   293	        self.filter_map(|s| s.into_string().ok()).collect()
   294	    }
   295	}
   296	
   297	impl<T: Iterator<Item = OsString> + Sized> Args for T {}
   298	
   299	/// Returns an iterator over the command line arguments as `OsString`s.
   300	/// args_os() can be expensive to call
   301	pub fn args_os() -> impl Iterator<Item = OsString> {
   302	    ARGV.iter().cloned()
   303	}
   304	
   305	/// Read a line from stdin and check whether the first character is `'y'` or `'Y'`
   306	pub fn read_yes() -> bool {
   307	    let mut s = String::new();
   308	    match std::io::stdin().read_line(&mut s) {
   309	        Ok(_) => matches!(s.chars().next(), Some('y' | 'Y')),
   310	        _ => false,
   311	    }
   312	}
   313	
   314	/// Converts an `OsStr` to a UTF-8 `&[u8]`.
   315	///
   316	/// This always succeeds on unix platforms,
   317	/// and fails on other platforms if the string can't be coerced to UTF-8.
   318	pub fn os_str_as_bytes(os_string: &OsStr) -> mods::error::UResult<&[u8]> {
   319	    #[cfg(unix)]
   320	    let bytes = os_string.as_bytes();
   321	
   322	    #[cfg(not(unix))]
   323	    let bytes = os_string
   324	        .to_str()
   325	        .ok_or_else(|| {
   326	            mods::error::UUsageError::new(1, "invalid UTF-8 was detected in one or more arguments")
   327	        })?
   328	        .as_bytes();
   329	
   330	    Ok(bytes)
   331	}
   332	
   333	/// Performs a potentially lossy conversion from `OsStr` to UTF-8 bytes.
   334	///
   335	/// This is always lossless on unix platforms,
   336	/// and wraps [`OsStr::to_string_lossy`] on non-unix platforms.
   337	pub fn os_str_as_bytes_lossy(os_string: &OsStr) -> Cow<[u8]> {
   338	    #[cfg(unix)]
   339	    let bytes = Cow::from(os_string.as_bytes());
   340	
   341	    #[cfg(not(unix))]
   342	    let bytes = match os_string.to_string_lossy() {
   343	        Cow::Borrowed(slice) => Cow::from(slice.as_bytes()),
   344	        Cow::Owned(owned) => Cow::from(owned.into_bytes()),
   345	    };
   346	
   347	    bytes
   348	}
   349	
   350	/// Converts a `&[u8]` to an `&OsStr`,
   351	/// or parses it as UTF-8 into an [`OsString`] on non-unix platforms.
   352	///
   353	/// This always succeeds on unix platforms,
   354	/// and fails on other platforms if the bytes can't be parsed as UTF-8.
   355	pub fn os_str_from_bytes(bytes: &[u8]) -> mods::error::UResult<Cow<'_, OsStr>> {
   356	    #[cfg(unix)]
   357	    let os_str = Cow::Borrowed(OsStr::from_bytes(bytes));
   358	    #[cfg(not(unix))]
   359	    let os_str = Cow::Owned(OsString::from(str::from_utf8(bytes).map_err(|_| {
   360	        mods::error::UUsageError::new(1, "Unable to transform bytes into OsStr")
   361	    })?));
   362	
   363	    Ok(os_str)
   364	}
   365	
   366	/// Converts a `Vec<u8>` into an `OsString`, parsing as UTF-8 on non-unix platforms.
   367	///
   368	/// This always succeeds on unix platforms,
   369	/// and fails on other platforms if the bytes can't be parsed as UTF-8.
   370	pub fn os_string_from_vec(vec: Vec<u8>) -> mods::error::UResult<OsString> {
   371	    #[cfg(unix)]
   372	    let s = OsString::from_vec(vec);
   373	    #[cfg(not(unix))]
   374	    let s = OsString::from(String::from_utf8(vec).map_err(|_| {
   375	        mods::error::UUsageError::new(1, "invalid UTF-8 was detected in one or more arguments")
   376	    })?);
   377	
   378	    Ok(s)
   379	}
   380	
   381	/// Converts an `OsString` into a `Vec<u8>`, parsing as UTF-8 on non-unix platforms.
   382	///
   383	/// This always succeeds on unix platforms,
   384	/// and fails on other platforms if the bytes can't be parsed as UTF-8.
   385	pub fn os_string_to_vec(s: OsString) -> mods::error::UResult<Vec<u8>> {
   386	    #[cfg(unix)]
   387	    let v = s.into_vec();
   388	    #[cfg(not(unix))]
   389	    let v = s
   390	        .into_string()
   391	        .map_err(|_| {
   392	            mods::error::UUsageError::new(1, "invalid UTF-8 was detected in one or more arguments")
   393	        })?
   394	        .into();
   395	
   396	    Ok(v)
   397	}
   398	
   399	/// Equivalent to `std::BufRead::lines` which outputs each line as a `Vec<u8>`,
   400	/// which avoids panicking on non UTF-8 input.
   401	pub fn read_byte_lines<R: std::io::Read>(
   402	    mut buf_reader: BufReader<R>,
   403	) -> impl Iterator<Item = Vec<u8>> {
   404	    iter::from_fn(move || {
   405	        let mut buf = Vec::with_capacity(256);
   406	        let size = buf_reader.read_until(b'\n', &mut buf).ok()?;
   407	
   408	        if size == 0 {
   409	            return None;
   410	        }
   411	
   412	        // Trim (\r)\n
   413	        if buf.ends_with(b"\n") {
   414	            buf.pop();
   415	            if buf.ends_with(b"\r") {
   416	                buf.pop();
   417	            }
   418	        }
   419	
   420	        Some(buf)
   421	    })
   422	}
   423	
   424	/// Equivalent to `std::BufRead::lines` which outputs each line as an `OsString`
   425	/// This won't panic on non UTF-8 characters on Unix,
   426	/// but it still will on Windows.
   427	pub fn read_os_string_lines<R: std::io::Read>(
   428	    buf_reader: BufReader<R>,
   429	) -> impl Iterator<Item = OsString> {
   430	    read_byte_lines(buf_reader).map(|byte_line| os_string_from_vec(byte_line).expect("UTF-8 error"))
   431	}

   433	/// Prompt the user with a formatted string and returns `true` if they reply `'y'` or `'Y'`
   434	///
   435	/// This macro functions accepts the same syntax as `format!`. The prompt is written to
   436	/// `stderr`. A space is also printed at the end for nice spacing between the prompt and
   437	/// the user input. Any input starting with `'y'` or `'Y'` is interpreted as `yes`.
   438	///
   439	/// # Examples
   440	/// ```
   441	/// use uucore::prompt_yes;
   442	/// let file = "foo.rs";
   443	/// prompt_yes!("Do you want to delete '{file}'?");
   444	/// ```
   445	/// will print something like below to `stderr` (with `util_name` substituted by the actual
   446	/// util name) and will wait for user input.
   447	/// ```txt
   448	/// util_name: Do you want to delete 'foo.rs'?
   449	/// ```
   450	#[macro_export]
   451	macro_rules! prompt_yes(
   452	    ($($args:tt)+) => ({
   453	        use std::io::Write;
   454	        eprint!("{}: ", uucore::util_name());
   455	        eprint!($($args)+);
   456	        eprint!(" ");
   457	        let res = std::io::stderr().flush().map_err(|err| {
   458	            $crate::error::USimpleError::new(1, err.to_string())
   459	        });
   460	        uucore::show_if_err!(res);
   461	        uucore::read_yes()
   462	    })
   463	);
   464	
   465	/// Represent either a character or a byte.
   466	/// Used to iterate on partially valid UTF-8 data
   467	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
   468	pub enum CharByte {
   469	    Char(char),
   470	    Byte(u8),
   471	}
   472	
   473	impl From<char> for CharByte {
   474	    fn from(value: char) -> Self {
   475	        CharByte::Char(value)
   476	    }
   477	}
   478	
   479	impl From<u8> for CharByte {
   480	    fn from(value: u8) -> Self {
   481	        CharByte::Byte(value)
   482	    }
   483	}
   484	
   485	impl From<&u8> for CharByte {
   486	    fn from(value: &u8) -> Self {
   487	        CharByte::Byte(*value)
   488	    }
   489	}

use std::io::{self, Write};

fn main() {
    let stdout = io::stdout();
    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
    
    // Simulate what cat does when reading from /dev/zero
    let data = [0u8; 4096];
    
    // Try to write a large amount of data quickly
    for _ in 0..1000 {
        match stdout_lock.write_all(&data) {
            Ok(_) => {},
            Err(e) => {
                if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
                    // Exit cleanly
                    std::process::exit(0);
                } else {
                    eprintln!("Unexpected error: {}", e);
                    std::process::exit(1);
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    // Try to flush
    if let Err(e) = stdout_lock.flush() {
        if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
            std::process::exit(0);
        } else {
            eprintln!("Flush error: {}", e);
            std::process::exit(1);
        }
    }
}'

+// Debug script to understand where the EPIPE error is coming from
+
+use std::io::{self, Write};
+
+fn main() {
+    let stdout = io::stdout();
+    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
+    
+    // Simulate what cat does when reading from /dev/zero
+    let data = [0u8; 4096];
+    
+    // Try to write a large amount of data quickly
+    for _ in 0..1000 {
+        match stdout_lock.write_all(&data) {
+            Ok(_) => {},
+            Err(e) => {
+                if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+                    // Exit cleanly
+                    std::process::exit(0);
+                } else {
+                    eprintln!("Unexpected error: {}", e);
+                    std::process::exit(1);
+                }
+            }
+        }
+    }
+    
+    // Try to flush
+    if let Err(e) = stdout_lock.flush() {
+        if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+            std::process::exit(0);
+        } else {
+            eprintln!("Flush error: {}", e);
+            std::process::exit(1);
+        }
+    }
+}

new file mode 100644

@@ -0,0 +1,104 @@
+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""Helper to fix all EPIPE handling in cat.rs"""
+
+import re
+
+def fix_write_operations(content):
+    """Fix write operations to handle EPIPE gracefully"""
+    
+    # Pattern to find write_all and flush calls that use `?` operator
+    # This indicates they're propagating errors but not handling EPIPE
+    patterns = [
+        r'(\s+)(\w+\.write_all\([^)]+\))\?',
+        r'(\s+)(\w+\.flush\(\))\?'
+    ]
+    
+    for pattern in patterns:
+        # Replace pattern with EPIPE handling
+        replacement = r'\1if let Err(e) = \2 {\n\1    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {\n\1        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat\n\1        return Ok(());\n\1    } else {\n\1        return Err(e.into());\n\1    }\n\1}'
+        content = re.sub(pattern, replacement, content)
+    
+    return content
+
+# Apply the fix
+with open('/testbed/src/uu/cat/src/cat.rs', 'r') as f:
+    content = f.read()
+
+# Fix the write operations we identified earlier
+content = content.replace('writer.write_all(b"\\r")?', '''if let Err(e) = writer.write_all(b"\\r") {
+                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
+                        return Ok(());
+                    } else {
+                        return Err(e.into());
+                    }
+                }''')
+
+content = content.replace('writer.write_all(b"^M")?', '''if let Err(e) = writer.write_all(b"^M") {
+                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
+                        return Ok(());
+                    } else {
+                        return Err(e.into());
+                    }
+                }''')
+
+content = content.replace('writer.flush()?', '''if let Err(e) = writer.flush() {
+                    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+                        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
+                        return Ok(());
+                    } else {
+                        return Err(e.into());
+                    }
+                }''')
+
+# Fix the write_end_of_line function
+old_write_end_of_line = '''fn write_end_of_line<W: Write>(
+    writer: &mut W,
+    end_of_line: &[u8],
+    is_interactive: bool,
+) -> CatResult<()> {
+    writer.write_all(end_of_line)?;
+    if is_interactive {
+        writer.flush()?;
+    }
+    Ok(())
+}'''
+
+new_write_end_of_line = '''fn write_end_of_line<W: Write>(
+    writer: &mut W,
+    end_of_line: &[u8],
+    is_interactive: bool,
+) -> CatResult<()> {
+    if let Err(e) = writer.write_all(end_of_line) {
+        if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+            // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
+            return Ok(());
+        } else {
+            return Err(e.into());
+        }
+    }
+    if is_interactive {
+        if let Err(e) = writer.flush() {
+            if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+                // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat
+                return Ok(());
+            } else {
+                return Err(e.into());
+            }
+        }
+    }
+    Ok(())
+}'''
+
+content = content.replace(old_write_end_of_line, new_write_end_of_line)
+
+# Fix line_number.write calls
+old_pattern = r'(\s+)state\.line_number\.write\(&mut writer\)\?'
+replacement = r'\1if let Err(e) = state.line_number.write(&mut writer) {\n\1    if e.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {\n\1        // Broken pipe - exit gracefully like GNU cat\n\1        return Ok(());\n\1    } else {\n\1        return Err(e.into());\n\1    }\n\1}'
+content = re.sub(old_pattern, replacement, content)
+
+with open('/testbed/src/uu/cat/src/cat.rs', 'w') as f:
+    f.write(content)
+
+print("Fixed EPIPE handling in cat.rs")
\ No newline at end of file

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""Test cat directly with different approaches"""
+
+import subprocess
+import time
+import os
+
+# Test simple cat with /dev/null
+cat_path = "/testbed/target/debug/coreutils"
+
+print("Test 1: cat /dev/null")
+result = subprocess.run([cat_path, "cat", "/dev/null"], capture_output=True, text=True)
+print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
+print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
+print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr.strip() if result.stderr else 'None'}")
+
+print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
+
+print("Test 2: cat - (stdin) with empty input")
+result = subprocess.run([cat_path, "cat", "-"], input="", capture_output=True, text=True)
+print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
+print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
+print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr.strip() if result.stderr else 'None'}")
+
+print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
+
+print("Test 3: GNU cat /dev/zero | head -c 10")
+result = subprocess.run("cat /dev/zero | head -c 10", shell=True, capture_output=True)
+print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
+print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
+print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr.decode() if result.stderr else 'None'}")
+
+print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
+
+# Test with timeout to prevent hanging
+print("Test 4: uutils cat /dev/zero | head -c 10 with timeout")
+try:
+    proc = subprocess.Popen(
+        [cat_path, "cat", "/dev/zero"], 
+        stdout=subprocess.PIPE, 
+        stderr=subprocess.PIPE
+    )
+    head_proc = subprocess.Popen(
+        ["head", "-c", "10"],
+        stdin=proc.stdout,
+        stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
+        stderr=subprocess.PIPE
+    )
+    
+    # Wait a bit
+    time.sleep(2)
+    
+    # Terminate cat if it's still running
+    if proc.poll() is None:
+        proc.terminate()
+        proc.wait()
+    
+    # Get output
+    stdout, stderr = head_proc.communicate()
+    
+    print(f"  Head stdout length: {len(stdout)}")
+    print(f"  Head stderr: {stderr.decode() if stderr else 'None'}")
+    print(f"  Head exit code: {head_proc.returncode}")
+    print(f"  Cat exit code: {proc.returncode}")
+    print(f"  Cat stderr: {proc.stderr.read().decode() if proc.stderr else 'None'}")
+    
+except Exception as e:
+    print(f"  Error: {e}")

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""Test script to reproduce the EPIPE issue with cat reading from /dev/zero"""
+
+import subprocess
+import os
+import sys
+
+def test_epipe_issue():
+    """Test if cat handles EPIPE error when reading from /dev/zero"""
+    
+    # Test 1: Normal cat /dev/zero | head -c 10
+    print("Test 1: cat /dev/zero | head -c 10")
+    try:
+        result = subprocess.run(
+            "cat /dev/zero | head -c 10",
+            shell=True,
+            capture_output=True,
+            text=True
+        )
+        print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
+        print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
+        print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr}")
+    except Exception as e:
+        print(f"  Error: {e}")
+    
+    print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
+    
+    # Test 2: Using uutils cat specifically
+    print("Test 2: Using uutils cat built from this repo")
+    
+    # Skip building - assume already built
+    print("Assuming uutils coreutils is already built...")
+    
+    # Test with uutils cat
+    cat_path = "/testbed/target/release/coreutils"
+    
+    if not os.path.exists(cat_path):
+        # Try debug build
+        cat_path = "/testbed/target/debug/coreutils"
+        if not os.path.exists(cat_path):
+            print("Could not find built coreutils binary")
+            return
+    
+    print(f"Using coreutils binary: {cat_path}")
+    
+    try:
+        result = subprocess.run(
+            f"{cat_path} cat /dev/zero | head -c 10",
+            shell=True,
+            capture_output=True,
+            text=True
+        )
+        print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
+        print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
+        if result.stderr:
+            print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr}")
+        else:
+            print("  No stderr output")
+    except Exception as e:
+        print(f"  Error: {e}")
+    
+    print("\n" + "="*50 + "\n")
+    
+    # Test 3: Compare with GNU cat
+    print("Test 3: Using GNU cat for comparison")
+    try:
+        result = subprocess.run(
+            "cat /dev/zero | head -c 10",
+            shell=True,
+            capture_output=True,
+            text=True
+        )
+        print(f"  Exit code: {result.returncode}")
+        print(f"  Stdout length: {len(result.stdout)}")
+        if result.stderr:
+            print(f"  Stderr: {result.stderr}")
+        else:
+            print("  No stderr output")
+    except Exception as e:
+        print(f"  Error: {e}")
+
+if __name__ == "__main__":
+    test_epipe_issue()

+// Test to understand EPIPE handling
+
+use std::io;
+use std::io::Write;
+
+fn main() {
+    // Check EPIPE error code

+    println!("EPIPE error: {}", epipe_error);
+    
+    // Check if we can match on error kind
+    match epipe_error.kind() {
+        io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe => {
+            println!("EPIPE matches ErrorKind::BrokenPipe");
+        }
+        _ => {
+            println!("EPIPE does not match BrokenPipe");
+        }
+    }

+// Test to see if EPIPE handling is working correctly
+
+use std::io::{self, Write};
+
+fn main() {
+    let stdout = io::stdout();
+    let mut stdout_lock = stdout.lock();
+    
+    // Test writing a single byte and handling EPIPE
+    let test_byte = [0u8];
+    
+    match stdout_lock.write_all(&test_byte) {
+        Ok(_) => println!("Write successful"),
+        Err(e) => {
+            if e.kind() == io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe {
+                println!("Got broken pipe error");
+                std::process::exit(0); // Exit cleanly like GNU cat
+            } else {
+                eprintln!("Error: {}", e);
+                std::process::exit(1);
+            }
+        }
+    }
+    
+    // If we get here, continue normally
+    println!("Continuing after write...");
+}

+#!/usr/bin/env python3
+"""Trace where the EPIPE error is coming from"""
+
+import subprocess
+import sys
+
+# Run the command and capture both stdout and stderr separately
+cat_path = "/testbed/target/debug/coreutils"
+
+print(f"Running: {cat_path} cat /dev/zero | head -c 10")
+
+# Use Popen to capture stderr separately 
+cat_process = subprocess.Popen(
+    [cat_path, "cat", "/dev/zero"],
+    stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
+    stderr=subprocess.PIPE
+)
+
+head_process = subprocess.Popen(
+    ["head", "-c", "10"],
+    stdin=cat_process.stdout,
+    stdout=subprocess.PIPE,
+    stderr=subprocess.PIPE
+)
+
+# Close the stdout of cat process
+cat_process.stdout.close()
+
+# Get the output
+head_output, head_stderr = head_process.communicate()
+
+# Get the stderr from cat process
+cat_stderr = cat_process.stderr.read()
+
+print(f"Head stdout length: {len(head_output)}")
+print(f"Head stderr: {head_stderr.decode() if head_stderr else 'None'}")
+print(f"Cat stderr: {cat_stderr.decode() if cat_stderr else 'None'}")
+print(f"Head exit code: {head_process.returncode}")
+print(f"Cat exit code: {cat_process.wait()}")
